href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F9809#tips?yhoo=1\"\u003Eoften with your help\u003C\u002Fa\u003E — \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com?yhoo=1\"\u003EFood52\u003C\u002Fa\u003E's Senior Editor Kristen Miglore is unearthing recipes that are nothing short of genius.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EToday: A wholesome, 4-ingredient DIY grenadine for better drinks at home — plus a gutsy technique for juicing a pomegranate without seeding first. This one’s for you, Shirley.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Frecipes\u002F26786-jeffrey-morgenthaler-s-diy-grenadine?yhoo=1\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002Fv9qi4r-ecUYrLdm2No0xzDVnSAE\" width=\"630\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI bet just about every one of us has happy childhood memories of Shirley Temples; of sweet, sharp fizz and glee; of feeling both childish and adult; of coveting cherries. There were \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpunchdrink.com\u002Fnews\u002Fpour-out-a-shirley-temple-for-shirley-temple\u002F\"\u003Enever enough cherries\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHow sad that none of the ingredients live up to our adult standards — literally not a one: ginger ale or 7-up, maraschinos the color of your \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.comfortkraft.com\u002Fimages\u002FM8240.gif\"\u003E80s culottes\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and tinted high fructose corn syrup masquerading as grenadine. Did you know grenadine is supposed to be pomegranate syrup, after \u003Cem\u003Egrenade\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, the French word for the fruit? Neither did I.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FKsJ9v1FLAmYMgD2f6_8rgsVpFIg\" width=\"630\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESo if you knew how outrageously easy it is to make your own — real, delicious, \u003Cem\u003Epomegranate\u003C\u002Fem\u003E — grenadine, you’d be drinking a lot more Shirley Temples. And pink, but classy, cocktails. Maybe even \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=ws-YqUcD0LY&amp;feature=kp\"\u003ETequila Sunrises\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. (No? Okay.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis recipe comes from \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002Fjeffmorgen\"\u003EJeffery Morgenthaler\u003C\u002Fa\u003E — one of the best mixologists (and&nbsp;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.jeffreymorgenthaler.com\u002F\"\u003Edrinks bloggers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) in the country — and has 4 ingredients. You could have made it just now instead of reading the last 3 paragraphs (sorry).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002Fjeffmorgen\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Jeffrey Morgenthaler\" height=\"400\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FJjyTvX8mk0ym9eEzFDH903BOAQQ\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&quot;I developed the recipe in response to what I saw as so many other bartenders over-thinking the syrup and using all sorts of bizarre ingredients, strange techniques, and other odd methods,&quot; Morgenthaler told me.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere are a couple ways to go about it. At the low-investment end of the spectrum, you can buy a bottle of 100% pomegranate juice.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThen making grenadine is only a matter of warming up the juice, stirring in some raw sugar, pomegranate molasses, and orange flower water — which, if your pantry is well-stocked, you probably already have. If not, hit up Whole Foods, your local Middle Eastern market, or the internet.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EMore:&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F3890-unsung-ingredient-pomegranate-molasses?yhoo=1\"\u003ESee what else you can do with that bottle of pomegranate molasses\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FGYvMMHM7i1kqaGMzSMR1QRQXtO8\" width=\"630\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIf you want to go even more DIY, you can juice your own pomegranates. There are a number of ways you can do this — but most involve plucking the arils from their spongy catacombs first, then blending and straining. As Louisa Shafia writes in \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fprovisions\u002Fproducts\u002F689-the-new-persian-kitchen-signed-cookbook?yhoo=1\"\u003EThe New Persian Kitchen\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, “The successful accomplishment of this operation is a topic shrouded in mystery and confusion.”\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002F3TBAjjQ6TPJFn6v7RKIUkG2RNAc\" width=\"48%\"\u003E&nbsp; \u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FFUuM2Hc3lOfDEpwxdjkXPd05viA\" width=\"48%\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EInstead, you can do as Morgenthaler does, and just juice the whole lot in your juicer — if it fits a half a grapefruit, it fits a half a pomegranate.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FiQG1ZL4CivuyWZSsmy18HuAo_hc\" width=\"630\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYou might have one of these&nbsp;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fprovisions\u002Fproducts\u002F538-citrus-press-silver-matte?yhoo=1\"\u003Efancy contraptions\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, or you might just have a&nbsp;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fprovisions\u002Fproducts\u002F793-ceramic-juicer?yhoo=1\"\u003Esmall manual version\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Either will work.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002Fb734-q4KFrecdT5kkq1nYKB4czI\" width=\"48%\"\u003E&nbsp; \u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002Fkv0TJzOz0GivFVpcHzBjTEzaeRU\" width=\"48%\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESome arils will fall away unbreached, but just pass it all through a strainer, crushing any lingering juice out with the back of a sturdy spoon. Put on an apron (or wear black) to be safe, but juicing a halved pomegranate is surprisingly contained.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EChoose your juicing method depending on your constitution and what sorts of kitchen chores you like best. (And if you don’t like any, revisit option 1 above.) I’d rather mash fruit and watch a river of juice stream out than get out my blender; you might feel differently.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FdOhGhVh5Eu64-adFv3DvGC6FBkc\" width=\"48%\"\u003E&nbsp; \u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FZgvg87oPXN7Us766iFSN4OgawcU\" width=\"48%\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FpprhUQ6F0FkkOJ_l-RB-jXUE_Wc\" width=\"48%\"\u003E&nbsp; \u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FreTMfOs4RguAH5pU1FApXTj0pb8\" width=\"48%\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThat’s it — you have homemade grenadine. Stir it into sparkling water, pour it over ice cream and yogurt and cake, explore your bar.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt would take longer to walk down the aisle in the liquor store to find bad grenadine than it does to make the good stuff from scratch. And you will have a batch that will last you for a very long time, unless you have a household that’s particularly fiendish for Zombie Punch.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EPut the rest in your fridge. \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F7372-grappa-cherries?yhoo=1\"\u003EStock up on cherries.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Frecipes\u002F26786-jeffrey-morgenthaler-s-diy-grenadine?yhoo=1\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"DIY Grenadine from Food52\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FUQTN03J68jJ4TIYySXF7ilAv01M\" width=\"630\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Frecipes\u002F26786-jeffrey-morgenthaler-s-diy-grenadine?yhoo=1\"\u003EJeffrey Morgenthaler’s DIY Grenadine\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EAdapted slightly from \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.jeffreymorgenthaler.com\"\u003EJeffrey Morgenthaler\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EMakes about 1 quart\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E2 cups fresh pomegranate juice (two to four large pomegranates) or 100% pomegranate juice\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E \u003Cstrong\u003Elike\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E \u003Cstrong\u003EPOM Wonderful\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E2 cups unbleached sugar\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E2 fluid ounces (1\u002F4 cup) pomegranate molasses\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E1 teaspoon orange blossom water\u003Ca\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca The Secret to Understanding Sausage","summary":"Hold up! You’re (probably) thinking about sausage all wrong.  ","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FAZFZeZE7SoZEjrbb_aiGUzwpKUE\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EPhoto credit: Getty\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHold up! You’re (probably) thinking about \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Frigatoni-with-sausage-peas-and-fresh-ricotta-78855604783.html\"\u003Esausage\u003C\u002Fa\u003E all wrong.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThat’s the takeaway from a gorgeous&nbsp;forthcoming cookbook by San Francisco butcher shop \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002F4505meats.com\u002F\"\u003E4505 Meats\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&nbsp;aptly titled, “Sausage Making: The Definitive Guide with Recipes.” The book covers recipes for every type of sausage you might desire, plus a few decadent extras like pig’s head terrine and sausage-stuffed suckling pig.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&quot;For us, texture is how we determine the differences between sausages,&quot; said Ryan Farr, the chef, butcher, and owner behind 4505 explained. &quot;We think: Do we want something smooth like a hot dog or coarse like a breakfast sausage?&nbsp;Each texture in the book has a master ratio to it: meat to salt to water. Once you master that texture, you can add any flavor you want.”\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut you can’t, for instance, just say you want a Spanish sausage and expect your butcher to know what you’re talking about.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&quot;Even in Spain, there are so many different regions [of sausage-making]; it’s almost like barbecue,&quot; Farr explained. &quot;A lot of the things are determining the nuts and bolts of a sausage, including flavor and style of cooking.&quot;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ERather than trying to understand the nuances that set apart dozens of types of sausage around the world,&nbsp;Farr believes it’s easier to first understand the four basic types of sausage textures. “You can make any kind of sausage that you want as long as you know these different style textures,” he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWithout further ado, the sausage:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002F_TTALV6ygqzShewlqJQ8x6o1gY4\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EPhoto credit: Chronicle Books\u002FEd Anderson\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ECoarse sausage is the most basic kind of sausage. Its texture is crumbly and a little dry, and the sausages often doesn’t have a casing; they’re simply browned in a pan. Coarse sausages include the&nbsp;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fshine.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Frecipes\u002Ffresh-breakfast-sausage-338460-mslo.html;_ylt=AwrBEiITKR5T3lYAPQaDmolQ\"\u003Ebreakfast sausage\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&nbsp;you might eat alongside pancakes and maple syrup, spicy Spanish chorizo, and spiced Middle Eastern merguez sausage.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FkDKPORXxGkeka1Ggl5SAK5lDT0Q\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EPhoto credit: Chronicle Books\u002FEd Anderson\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EJuicy, soft-textured sausages contain a higher percentage of liquid and fat than coarse or firm-textured sausages. Unlike smooth sausages, the meat is only lightly mixed, not&nbsp;pure?ed. Also, they tend to be poached rather than smoked or grilled. This category includes sausages like&nbsp;\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.foodandwine.com\u002Frecipes\u002Fboudin-blanc-with-leeks-and-mustard-sauce\"\u003Eboudin blanc\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, (the&nbsp;French sausage of veal and pork), Cajun \u003Cem\u003Eboudin\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (made with pork liver and rice), and Scottish white pudding (a beef and pork-based sausage with rolled oats).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs1.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002FxDEnwZY1eMhHRYZzwhqiPOErnhw\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EPhoto credit: Chronicle Books\u002FEd Anderson\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.saveur.com\u002Farticle\u002FKitchen\u002FSaveur-100-2011-Housemade-Kielbasa\"\u003EKielbasa\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fshine.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Frecipes\u002Fmidwestern-grilled-bratwurst-sandwiches-with-caraway-sauerkraut-312459-mslo.html;_ylt=AwrBJR9SLR5T43UAdwODmolQ\"\u003Ebratwurst\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and the Portuguese&nbsp;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fshine.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Frecipes\u002Fcuban-spiced-chicken-thighs-with-chorizo-and-rice-236875-epicurious.html;_ylt=AwrBEiFkLR5TLwIAESKDmolQhttp:\u002F\u002Fshine.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Frecipes\u002Fcuban-spiced-chicken-thighs-with-chorizo-and-rice-236875-epicurious.html;_ylt=AwrBEiFkLR5TLwIAESKDmolQ\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003Elingui&ccedil;a\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&nbsp;are all firm sausages; they are tight links that contain little water compared to soft sausages. They’re usually all-meat, without vegetables or other fillers, and are often smoked.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002Foriginal\u002Fp0YO8epVRA-FRK_V6p_7O8q71Ec\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EPhoto credit: Chronicle Books\u002FEd Anderson\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESmooth sausages include \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fshine.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Frecipes\u002Fvietnamese-chicken-sandwich-banh-mi-241475-epicurious.html;_ylt=AwrBEiETMR5TSHkAWTaDmolQ\"\u003Eliverwurst\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, blood bologna, and even your all-American, all-beef \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Fode-to-the-1-25-hot-dog-72887274917.html\"\u003Ehot dogs\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. They’re also the most difficult to make. This is because the meat, which contains a higher percentage of liquid than other types of sausage, must first be pure?ed in a food processor until it reaches a smooth and creamy consistency. It also has to be kept cool the entire time, otherwise your sausages will wind up with a grainy texture.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHungry for sausage yet? Yeah.         /* These next few are necessary because pushState()
         * doesn't update the referrer automatically.
         */
        lastUrl: null,

        setLastUrl: function(url) {
            this.lastUrl = url;
        },

        getLastUrl: function() {
            return (this.lastUrl == null) ? document.referrer : this.lastUrl;
        },


        getContentType: function(type) {
            var ct;
            switch (type) {
                case 'photoset':
                    ct = 4;
                    break;
                case 'story':
                    ct = 1;
                    break;
                case 'video':
                    ct = 3;
                    break;
                case 'image':
                    ct = 8;
                    break;
                case 'quote':
                    ct = 18;
                    break;
            }
            return ct;
        },

        beaconPageview: function(magazine, rapidKeys) {
            rapidKeys["_w"]  = document.location.href;
            YAHOO.i13n.doComscoreStuff(magazine, App.Cache.spaceId);
            rapidKeys['lurl'] = this.getLastUrl();
            if (!this.rapid) {
                this._initRapid(rapidKeys);
                this._maybeClearMaybeRapids();
            } else {
                this._maybeClearMaybeRapids();
                this.rapid.beaconPageview(rapidKeys);
            }
        },

        _lastPageView: null,

        beaconArticleview: function(magazine, article, cat) {
            this.beaconPageview(magazine, {
                pt: 4,
                pd: 'article',
                pstcat: cat,
                pct: this.getContentType(article.get('type')),
                pstaid: article.get('ccm_id'),
                site: magazine,
                mrkt: 'US',
                ver: 'mags-' + App.Cache.version,
                lang: 'en-US'
            });
            var val = magazine;
            if (cat) {
                val += ':' + cat;
            }
            if (!this._lastPageView) {
                this._lastPageView = val;
            }
        },

        beaconHomepageView: function(magazine) {
            this.beaconPageview(magazine, {
                pt: 2,
                pd: 'index',
                site: magazine,
                mrkt: 'US',
                ver: 'mags-' + App.Cache.version,
                lang: 'en-US'
            });
            if (!this._lastPageView || this._lastPageView !== magazine) {
                this._removeAllTrackedModules();
                this._lastPageView = magazine;
            }
        },

        beaconTaggedView: function(magazine, tag) {
            this.beaconPageview(magazine, {
                pt: 3,
                pd: 'tag',
                pstcat: tag,
                pstaid: tag,
                site: magazine,
                mrkt: 'US',
                ver: 'mags-' + App.Cache.version,
                lang: 'en-US'
            });
            var val = magazine + ':' + tag;
            if (!this._lastPageView || this._lastPageView !== val) {
                this._removeAllTrackedModules();
                this._lastPageView = val;
            }
        },

        beaconAuthorView: function(magazine, author) {
            this.beaconPageview(magazine, {
                pt: 3,
                pd: 'author',
                pstcat: author,
                pstaid: author,
                site: magazine,
                mrkt: 'US',
                ver: 'mags-' + App.Cache.version,
                lang: 'en-US'
            });
            var val = magazine + ':' + author;
            if (!this._lastPageView || this._lastPageView !== val) {
                this._removeAllTrackedModules();
                this._lastPageView = val;
            }
        },

        _maybeRapids: [],

        _maybeRapidSomething: function(name, args) {
            if (this.rapid) {
                this.rapid[name].apply(this.rapid, args);
            } else {
                this._maybeRapids.push([name, args]);
                console.warn('delaying rapid call for ' + name);
            }
        },

        _maybeClearMaybeRapids: function() {
            if (this.rapid) {
                while (this._maybeRapids.length > 0) {
                    var c = this._maybeRapids.shift();
                    console.warn('fulfilling rapid call for ' + c[0]);
                    this._maybeRapidSomething(c[0], c[1]);
                }
            }
        },

        _addedModules: {},

        removeModule: function(module) {
            if (this._addedModules[module]) {
                this._maybeRapidSomething('removeModule', [module]);
                this._addedModules[module] = false;
            }
        },

        _removeAllTrackedModules: function() {
            for (var module in this._addedModules) {
                this.removeModule(module);
            }
        },

        module: function(module) {
            if (this._addedModules[module]) {
                this._maybeRapidSomething('refreshModule', [module]);
            } else {
                this._maybeRapidSomething('addModules', [module]);
                this._addedModules[module] = true;
            }
        },

        beaconEvent: function() {
            this._maybeRapidSomething('beaconEvent', arguments);
        },

        beaconClick: function() {
            this._maybeRapidSomething('beaconClick', arguments);
        }

    };

","body":"<p><img src=\"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/eGLrVbT54bM122W1RuVMeqiKuoY\"></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit: StockFood</em></p> \n<p>You saw that headline and rolled your eyes, didn’t you? You’ve seen the promise of “elegant <em>and </em>easy!” fail to deliver one too many times, the last of which ended with both egg yolk <em>and</em> lipstick stains on your skirt.</p> \n<p>Well, our promises, and our headlines, are true. Open up your hand, and let us take it; then, we will descend together into the wonderfully relaxed world of the chic, no-frills brunch. It only takes five steps.</p> \n<p><strong>Send paper invitations.</strong> While we’re down for the casual, “Hey, come on over” phone call, you’re going for elegance, here. Send a Real Invite. Like, via snail mail. Your friends will open their mailboxes, huffing and puffing their ways through bills, and suddenly, they’ll come upon a hand-written note. They’ll open it and smile immediately, whether they’re free to attend or not. The card doesn’t have to be made for an event invite, either; we like these blank ones from <a href=\"http://riflepaperco.com/item/Marigold_Blooms_Card/204/c34\">Rifle Paper Company</a>, and vintage postcards picked up from antique stores. (That’s right, they don’t even have to have envelopes!)</p> \n<p><strong>Let the food take the backseat.</strong> It should be tasty, of course, but it need not be fancy. What people want on a late weekend morning are hearty, simple dishes like frittatas and <a href=\"http://www.countrycrock.com/recipes/detail/34944/1/asparagus-peas-swiss-cheese-casserole\">vegetable casseroles</a>&nbsp;and hunks of yeasty bread with <a href=\"http://shine.yahoo.com/food/recipes/mixed-berry-jam-924847-mslo.html;_ylt=AwrSyCNpNPFSPmQAaA.DmolQ\">really good jam</a>. And booze. <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/photo-credit-getty-images-prosecco-is-the-flour-68174983627.html\">Sparkly booze</a>.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>Step up your d</strong><em><strong>&eacute;</strong></em><strong>cor.</strong> The food is easy, so take some time with the table. Select some playfully mismatched dishes; wash and press your napkins; spring for a fresh bouquet; write up some place cards. Why not? This is where you can have some fun. <a href=\"http://www.fishseddy.com/\">Fish’s Eddy</a> is a great resource for cheap, cheeky wares.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>Do serve dessert.</strong> This is another way to make your guests feel special without breaking your back. People rarely eat dessert during the daytime—pretty much only on vacation or at brunch—and it’s easy, because you can do all your prep ahead of time. We vote <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/the-secret-ingredient-for-better-pies-its-in-your-69180091340.html\">pie</a> or <a href=\"http://shine.yahoo.com/food/recipes/grand-raspberry-trifle-318066-mslo.html;_ylt=AwrTWfzE8vNSuW0A2EGDmolQ\">trifle</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>The chicest thing you can wear is calm.</strong> As etiquette maven <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/things-emily-post-taught-us-that-we-really-oughtta-do-71657148132.html\">Emily Post</a> wrote, “The truly good host is gracious and unflappable, no matter what happens. The more you take things in stride and handle them gracefully, the better your guests will feel.” What’s more elegant than Breakfast Ideas (for People Who Usually Skip Breakfast)","summary":"But sometimes, it’s not that we don’t have time to scarf down a bowl of sugary breakfast cereal—we just don’t want to.","body":"<p>Yeah, yeah, yeah. We&nbsp;<em>know</em>&nbsp;breakfast is the most important meal of the day. So we’ve been told by nearly every mother, gym teacher, and nutritionist since the beginning of time. But sometimes, it’s not that we don’t have <em>time</em> to scarf down a bowl of sugary breakfast cereal—we just don’t <em>want</em> to. Sweet breakfasts are not our thing.</p> \n<p>If you’re the same way, here are some scrumptiously savory breakfasts…for folks who like life on the savory side. </p> \n<p><strong>1. Spinach Frittata</strong></p> \n<p><strong><img alt=\"image\" src=\"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/pN7SLwBKtStT1SKg5HPer9e-LUY\"></strong></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit: StockFood</em></p> \n<p>Beat a few eggs in a bowl and fold in chopped spinach, thinly chopped garlic, and a bit of dill. Pour the mixture into a greasedcast iron pan and bake the whole thing for six to eight minutes at 325 degrees. <em>Voil&agrave;</em><em>!</em> Frittata!</p> \n<p><strong>2. Shrimp and Grits</strong></p> \n<p>Yes, you&nbsp;<em>can</em>&nbsp;have shrimp for breakfast. Sizzle up some thick-cut bacon and a few shrimps before folding them into a bowl of hot, creamy grits. You’re in heaven.</p> \n<p><strong>3.&nbsp;English Muffin Sandwich with Sausage and Egg</strong></p> \n<p><strong><img src=\"https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/8ddmM5f47tzOFjCAWfEFlVShIPY\"></strong></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit: StockFood</em></p> \n<p>No need to go through a drive-thru for one of these. Butter two halves of a toasted muffin before using them to trap a (cooked!) breakfast sausage link split lengthwise and a fried egg.</p> \n<p><strong>4. Breakfast Grilled Cheese</strong></p> \n<p>Grilled cheese becomes&nbsp;<em>breakfast</em>&nbsp;grilled cheese with the simple addition of an over-easy egg. We favor nutty cheeses like&nbsp;Gruy&egrave;re and Comt<em>&eacute;</em>.</p> \n<p><strong>5. Crepes with Goat Cheese, Mushrooms and Asparagus</strong></p> \n<p><em><img alt=\"image\" src=\"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/sjC2WPCrA4YsPQllzl2PpqXR5XE\"></em></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit: Getty</em></p> \n<p>Saut&eacute;ed mushrooms and asparagus are a match made in heaven in light, buttery crepes slathered with rich goat cheese.</p> \n<p><strong>6. Savory Bread Pudding</strong></p> \n<p>Got a loaf of bread lying around? Don’t let it go to waste. Try a savory bread pudding like&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.epicurious.com/recipes/food/views/Savory-Bread-Pudding-with-Mushrooms-and-Parmesan-Cheese-236494\">this one</a>&nbsp;using Parmesan cheese, mushrooms, onions, celery, and bell peppers.</p> \n<p><strong>7. Breakfast Calzone</strong></p> \n<p>Wrap cooked ground sausage, ricotta, onion, shredded Parmesan, and mozzarella in a bit of pizza dough and bake the whole shebang for eight to 12 minutes at&nbsp;400 degrees. You’ll forget that calzones are associated with any other meal.</p> \n<p><strong>8. Cheddar and Chive Scones</strong></p> \n<p><strong><img alt=\"image\" src=\"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/gpBKDK_8ljmVE665qnxTArlegTM\"></strong></p> \n<p><em>Image credit: StockFood</em></p> \n<p>Savory scones are a thing! Doctor your&nbsp;<a href=\"http://allrecipes.com/recipe/scones/\">standard scone recipe</a>&nbsp;by adding cheddar cheese and chopped chives; just remember to leave out the sugar.</p> \n<p><strong>9. Savory Oatmeal</strong></p> \n<p>Newsflash: oatmeal doesn’t always have to be sweet. Prepare your oats as you usually do, but finish them with a splash of soy sauce, chopped scallions, and a fried egg.</p> \n<p><strong>10. Breakfast Tacos</strong></p> \n<p><em><img alt=\"image\" src=\"https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/toQNYNHCL4Xo7-wQSV6kF9E4NyI\"></em></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit:&nbsp;Unilever</em></p> \n<p>Bored by plain Jane scrambled eggs?&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.countrycrock.com/crockcountry/media/632187/simply-delicious\">Breakfast tacos are the answer</a>. Whisk together four eggs, two cups of spinach leaves, some chopped tomatoes, onions, and—if you’re a fan of heat—a few slices of&nbsp;jalape&ntilde;o. Add the mixture to a Country Crock Simply Delicious<em>–</em>greased skillet and stir until it’s cooked thoroughly. The best part: toss the scrambled eggs into a corn tortilla and garnish with cheddar cheese.</p> \n<p>You now officially love breakfast.</p>","leadImages":[{"url":"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w175/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":175,"height":133,"size_type":"175"},{"url":"https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w200/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":200,"height":152,"size_type":"200"},{"url":"https://s2.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w250/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":250,"height":190,"size_type":"250"},{"url":"https://s2.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w300/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":300,"height":227,"size_type":"300"},{"url":"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w350/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":350,"height":265,"size_type":"350"},{"url":"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w400/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":400,"height":303,"size_type":"400"},{"url":"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w450/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":450,"height":341,"size_type":"450"},{"url":"https://s2.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":500,"height":379,"size_type":"500"},{"url":"https://s3.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w550/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":550,"height":417,"size_type":"550"},{"url":"https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w600/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":600,"height":455,"size_type":"600"},{"url":"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w700/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":700,"height":531,"size_type":"700"},{"url":"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w800/f411bbe055cb60a54ec54358932dc9ce44d21819","type":"image/jpeg","width":800,"height":607,"size_type":"800"},{"url":"https:// ","body":"<p><img src=\"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/eGLrVbT54bM122W1RuVMeqiKuoY\"></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit: StockFood</em></p> \n<p>You saw that headline and rolled your eyes, didn’t you? You’ve seen the promise of “elegant <em>and </em>easy!” fail to deliver one too many times, the last of which ended with both egg yolk <em>and</em> lipstick stains on your skirt.</p> \n<p>Well, our promises, and our headlines, are true. Open up your hand, and let us take it; then, we will descend together into the wonderfully relaxed world of the chic, no-frills brunch. It only takes five steps.</p> \n<p><strong>Send paper invitations.</strong> While we’re down for the casual, “Hey, come on over” phone call, you’re going for elegance, here. Send a Real Invite. Like, via snail mail. Your friends will open their mailboxes, huffing and puffing their ways through bills, and suddenly, they’ll come upon a hand-written note. They’ll open it and smile immediately, whether they’re free to attend or not. The card doesn’t have to be made for an event invite, either; we like these blank ones from <a href=\"http://riflepaperco.com/item/Marigold_Blooms_Card/204/c34\">Rifle Paper Company</a>, and vintage postcards picked up from antique stores. (That’s right, they don’t even have to have envelopes!)</p> \n<p><strong>Let the food take the backseat.</strong> It should be tasty, of course, but it need not be fancy. What people want on a late weekend morning are hearty, simple dishes like frittatas and <a href=\"http://www.countrycrock.com/recipes/detail/34944/1/asparagus-peas-swiss-cheese-casserole\">vegetable casseroles</a>&nbsp;and hunks of yeasty bread with <a href=\"http://shine.yahoo.com/food/recipes/mixed-berry-jam-924847-mslo.html;_ylt=AwrSyCNpNPFSPmQAaA.DmolQ\">really good jam</a>. And booze. <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/photo-credit-getty-images-prosecco-is-the-flour-68174983627.html\">Sparkly booze</a>.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>Step up your d</strong><em><strong>&eacute;</strong></em><strong>cor.</strong> The food is easy, so take some time with the table. Select some playfully mismatched dishes; wash and press your napkins; spring for a fresh bouquet; write up some place cards. Why not? This is where you can have some fun. <a href=\"http://www.fishseddy.com/\">Fish’s Eddy</a> is a great resource for cheap, cheeky wares.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>Do serve dessert.</strong> This is another way to make your guests feel special without breaking your back. People rarely eat dessert during the daytime—pretty much only on vacation or at brunch—and it’s easy, because you can do all your prep ahead of time. We vote <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/the-secret-ingredient-for-better-pies-its-in-your-69180091340.html\">pie</a> or <a href=\"http://shine.yahoo.com/food/recipes/grand-raspberry-trifle-318066-mslo.html;_ylt=AwrTWfzE8vNSuW0A2EGDmolQ\">trifle</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>The chicest thing you can wear is calm.</strong> As etiquette maven <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/things-emily-post-taught-us-that-we-really-oughtta-do-71657148132.html\">Emily Post</a> wrote, “The truly good host is gracious and unflappable, no matter what happens. The more you take things in stride and handle them gracefully, the better your guests will feel.” What’s more elegant than Season with salt and pepper.","body":"<p><img src=\"https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/pXRH9PtQYqBgh062mdAgFjTcnjc\"></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit: Getty Images</em></p> \n<p>There’s keeping things simple—the classic trench, the weeknight chicken saut&eacute;—and then there is a rut. The same piece of toast and [insert your favorite topping here], morning after morning. While we would never suggest you abandon your tried-and-true approach to what is one of the purest, most pleasurable breakfast options on earth (praise toast!), sometimes innovation is in order.</p> \n<p>Toast is a place to let your imagination run wild. It can take on salty; it can take on sweet, even dinner leftovers can be a beautiful thing on a golden slice of bread. (It’s basically crostini, but in the morning, right?)</p> \n<p>But let’s not get ahead of ourselves.</p> \n<p><strong>Chocolate-Hazelnut Spread &amp; Banana</strong></p> \n<p>Bring this classic late-night snack combo into the light of day. It is <em>heaven </em>with a cup of coffee.</p> \n<p><strong>Avocado, Lemon Juice &amp; Salt</strong></p> \n<p>So simple, so ridiculously delicious. Scoop ripe avocado onto a piece of toast and gently mash-spread it with the back of your fork. Squeeze on lemon juice and scatter with sea salt.</p> \n<p><strong>Fig Jam &amp; Prosciutto</strong></p> \n<p>You know this works on a dinner party cheese board, but it makes just as great of a savory-sweet breakfast. If you want to go full-on savory, sub the fig jam for Country Crock Simply Delicious and throw a few sliced cornichons on top.</p> \n<p><strong>Hummus &amp; Sundried Tomatoes</strong></p> \n<p>It might seem strange, but hummus is the cornerstone of a traditional breakfast in some parts of the world. And it’s a perfect option for someone who prefers savory dishes in the AM.</p> \n<p><strong>Peanut Butter, Sliced Apple &amp; Honey</strong></p> \n<p>This one’s a classic, and for good reason. Creamy peanut butter meets tart-sweet sliced apples, and when the whole thing is drizzled with honey, it’s just so right.</p> \n<p><strong>Sliced Hardboiled Egg, Mayo &amp; Paprika</strong></p> \n<p>Like a deviled egg, deconstructed, and without all the work.</p> \n<p><strong>Cream Cheese &amp; Smoked Salmon</strong></p> \n<p>All that bagel just gets in the way.&nbsp; If you have some capers, perhaps some feathery dill, or a slice of tomato, all the better.</p> \n<p><strong>Country Crock Simply Delicious, Sliced Radishes &amp; Salt</strong></p> \n<p>Something happens when the assertive flavor of a radish meets mellow creaminess; it’s called magic.</p> \n<p><strong>Ricotta with Roasted Red Peppers</strong></p> \n<p>Spoon-spread some ricotta onto a piece of toast, then lay slices of roasted red peppers on top. (Drain the peppers first, if using jarred ones, and dab with a towel to remove excess moisture.) Season with salt and pepper.</p> \n<p><strong>Cream Cheese &amp; Hot Pepper Jelly</strong></p> \n<p>Another dinner party hit that deserves the morning spotlight. Bright, sweet-hot pepper jelly is the perfect foil to a healthy layer of cream Someone has taken the time to get up before you, cook them, toss the first one because it’s always horrible, and deliver crisp-edged discs of sweet dough to you in bed, at the table, or while you’re watching cartoons. (Come on, we’ve all been there.) Or maybe that person is you, and you love your people enough to ensure that they wake up to the scent of pancakes.</p> \n<p>There’s no need to eat plain Jane pancakes when there’s a whole world of options out there, though. Here are a few of our favorite flapjack add-ons, because while a good thing is good, why not go for great?&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>Bacon</strong></p> \n<p>Crumble bits of cooked bacon into the batter, or—if you’re feeling like a champ—pour batter over whole cooked slices. Bacon, syrup, pancakes, in one fell breakfast treat.</p> \n<p>&nbsp;<strong>Orange</strong></p> \n<p>If you’re a citrus fan, you can add bits of orange zest or a splash of juice to the batter itself. Maybe go for sugar or honey instead of syrup on this one; citrus and honey are familiar friends.</p> \n<p><strong>Chocolate Chips</strong></p> \n<p>Classic for a reason. Add as many as you want, again at the batter stage. And hold off on syrup; a flurry of powdered sugar and a fat slab of butter are the way to go, so you can more easily taste the chocolate.</p> \n<p><strong>Blueberries</strong></p> \n<p>You feel that much healthier when you get fruit into the batter, and blueberries add an excellent texture sensation—all juice and pop—when they are pancake-i-fied.</p> \n<p><strong>Raspberries</strong></p> \n<p>Raspberries add color, tartness and all-around delight. Be sure to chop them small or puree them. If you do the latter, add them to the batter with a tiny bit less liquid than you’d otherwise use.</p> \n<p><strong>Peaches</strong></p> \n<p>Peaches are the epitome of summer, and chopped small they lend textural interest and natural sweetness.</p> \n<p><strong>Bananas</strong></p> \n<p>Rare is the child who doesn’t flip for a banana pancake. Adults have a tough time resisting their charms, too. Slice the bananas thin, adding them to the pancake while on the griddle for looks. You can also mince them and add them to the batter, if you prefer.</p> \n<p><strong>Ricotta</strong></p> \n<p>There’s an inimitable lightness to a ricotta pancake; try swapping out the milk in the recipe below for ricotta, and drizzle in a bit of milk if the batter looks too thick. Top them with honey or a spoonful more of ricotta, hit with a light dusting of black pepper. (Trust us.)</p> \n<p><strong>Eggnog</strong></p> \n<p>Around the winter holidays, swap the milk portion of your recipe for eggnog. Garnish with grated nutmeg and cinnamon for the most Christmas-y brunch we can imagine.</p> \n<p><strong>Granola</strong></p> \n<p>Quick pancakes get a wholesome (and just the right amount of hearty) with <a href=\"http://www.countrycrock.com/crockcountry/media/632187/simply-delicious\">oatmeal</a>, walnuts, honey and cinnamon.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>Basic Pancakes</strong></p> \n<p>Makes 12-15 pancakes</p> \n<p>1 cup all-purpose flour</p> \n<p>2 tablespoons sugar</p> \n<p>2 teaspoons baking powder</p> \n<p>1/2 teaspoon salt</p> \n<p>1 cup milk</p> \n<p>2 tablespoons unsalted butter, melted, or vegetable oil</p> \n<p>1 large egg</p> \n<p>1 tablespoon vegetable oil&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Whisk together flour, sugar, baking powder, and salt in a small bowl; set aside. Preheat oven to 200 degrees if you need to keep cooked pancakes warm.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Whisk together milk, butter (or oil), and egg in a medium-sized bowl. Add dry ingredients to milk mixture and whisk together until just moistened. Be careful not to&nbsp;over mix; a few lumps are totally fine.&nbsp;Heat a large skillet (nonstick or cast-iron) or griddle over medium-high heat. Very lightly oil skillet. Spoon 2 to 3 tablespoons of batter onto skillet for each pancake, using the back of the spoon to spread batter into a round.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Cook until pancakes show a few bubbles, of which some have burst, 1 to 2 minutes. Flip using a thin spatula, and cook until browned on the bottom, 1 to 2 minutes more. If needed, transfer pancakes to a baking sheet or platter; cover loosely with aluminum foil, and keep warm in oven. Continue with more oil and the rest of the batter.</p> \n<p></p> ","body":"<p><img src=\"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/eGLrVbT54bM122W1RuVMeqiKuoY\"></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit: StockFood</em></p> \n<p>You saw that headline and rolled your eyes, didn’t you? You’ve seen the promise of “elegant <em>and </em>easy!” fail to deliver one too many times, the last of which ended with both egg yolk <em>and</em> lipstick stains on your skirt.</p> \n<p>Well, our promises, and our headlines, are true. Open up your hand, and let us take it; then, we will descend together into the wonderfully relaxed world of the chic, no-frills brunch. It only takes five steps.</p> \n<p><strong>Send paper invitations.</strong> While we’re down for the casual, “Hey, come on over” phone call, you’re going for elegance, here. Send a Real Invite. Like, via snail mail. Your friends will open their mailboxes, huffing and puffing their ways through bills, and suddenly, they’ll come upon a hand-written note. They’ll open it and smile immediately, whether they’re free to attend or not. The card doesn’t have to be made for an event invite, either; we like these blank ones from <a href=\"http://riflepaperco.com/item/Marigold_Blooms_Card/204/c34\">Rifle Paper Company</a>, and vintage postcards picked up from antique stores. (That’s right, they don’t even have to have envelopes!)</p> \n<p><strong>Let the food take the backseat.</strong> It should be tasty, of course, but it need not be fancy. What people want on a late weekend morning are hearty, simple dishes like frittatas and <a href=\"http://www.countrycrock.com/recipes/detail/34944/1/asparagus-peas-swiss-cheese-casserole\">vegetable casseroles</a>&nbsp;and hunks of yeasty bread with <a href=\"http://shine.yahoo.com/food/recipes/mixed-berry-jam-924847-mslo.html;_ylt=AwrSyCNpNPFSPmQAaA.DmolQ\">really good jam</a>. And booze. <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/photo-credit-getty-images-prosecco-is-the-flour-68174983627.html\">Sparkly booze</a>.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>Step up your d</strong><em><strong>&eacute;</strong></em><strong>cor.</strong> The food is easy, so take some time with the table. Select some playfully mismatched dishes; wash and press your napkins; spring for a fresh bouquet; write up some place cards. Why not? This is where you can have some fun. <a href=\"http://www.fishseddy.com/\">Fish’s Eddy</a> is a great resource for cheap, cheeky wares.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>Do serve dessert.</strong> This is another way to make your guests feel special without breaking your back. People rarely eat dessert during the daytime—pretty much only on vacation or at brunch—and it’s easy, because you can do all your prep ahead of time. We vote <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/the-secret-ingredient-for-better-pies-its-in-your-69180091340.html\">pie</a> or <a href=\"http://shine.yahoo.com/food/recipes/grand-raspberry-trifle-318066-mslo.html;_ylt=AwrTWfzE8vNSuW0A2EGDmolQ\">trifle</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>The chicest thing you can wear is calm.</strong> As etiquette maven <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/food/things-emily-post-taught-us-that-we-really-oughtta-do-71657148132.html\">Emily Post</a> wrote, “The truly good host is gracious and unflappable, no matter what happens. The more you take things in stride and handle them gracefully, the better your guests will feel.” What’s more elegant than that?</p>","leadImages":[{"url":"https://s3.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w175/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":175,"height":117,"size_type":"175"},{"url":"https://s2.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w200/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":200,"height":133,"size_type":"200"},{"url":"https://s3.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w250/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":250,"height":167,"size_type":"250"},{"url":"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w300/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":300,"height":200,"size_type":"300"},{"url":"https://s1.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w350/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":350,"height":233,"size_type":"350"},{"url":"https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w400/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":400,"height":266,"size_type":"400"},{"url":"https://s3.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w450/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":450,"height":300,"size_type":"450"},{"url":"https://s2.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":500,"height":333,"size_type":"original"}],"lead_image":{"url":"https://s2.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/a195f8e12e02006ce9420e0a3cfc18bce89c3de2","type":"image/jpeg","width":500,"height":333,"size_type":"original"},"currentlySponsored":true},{"id":"a75929230068","magazine":"food","priority":"normal","palette":["#bed7dc","#eefbf8","#dbdbcb","#d0c8a6","#d3b059"],"tags":[{"tag":"breakfast","ts_update":1393469226,"name":"Breakfast","slug":"breakfast","count":50},{"tag":"simply-delicious","ts_update":1393469266,"name":"Simply We&nbsp;<em>know</em>&nbsp;breakfast is the most important meal of the day. So we’ve been told by nearly every mother, gym teacher, and nutritionist since the beginning of time. But sometimes, it’s not that we don’t have <em>time</em> to scarf down a bowl of sugary breakfast cereal—we just don’t <em>want</em> to. Sweet breakfasts are not our thing.</p> \n<p>If you’re the same way, here are some scrumptiously savory breakfasts…for folks who like life on the savory side. </p> \n<p><strong>1. Pour the mixture into a greasedcast iron pan and bake the whole thing for six to eight minutes at 325 degrees. <em>Voil&agrave;</em><em>!</em> Frittata!</p> \n<p><strong>2. Shrimp and Grits</strong></p> \n<p>Yes, you&nbsp;<em>can</em>&nbsp;have shrimp for breakfast. Sizzle up some thick-cut bacon and a few shrimps before folding them into a bowl of hot, creamy grits. You’re in heaven.</p> \n<p><strong>3.&nbsp;English Muffin Sandwich with Sausage and Egg</strong></p> \n<p><strong><img src=\"https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/original/8ddmM5f47tzOFjCAWfEFlVShIPY\"></strong></p> \n<p><em>Photo credit: StockFood</em></p> \n<p>No need to go through a drive-thru for one of these. Butter two halves of a toasted muffin before using them to trap a (cooked!) breakfast sausage link split lengthwise and a fried egg.</p> \n<p><strong>4. Breakfast Grilled Cheese</strong></p> \n<p>Grilled cheese becomes&nbsp;<em>breakfast</em>&nbsp;grilled cheese with the simple addition of an over-easy egg. We favor nutty cheeses like&nbsp;Gruy&egrave;re and Comt<em>&eacute;</em>.</p> \n<p><strong>5. Savory Bread Pudding</strong></p> \n<p>Got a loaf of bread lying around? Don’t let it go to waste. Try a savory bread pudding like&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.epicurious.com/recipes/food/views/Savory-Bread-Pudding-with-Mushrooms-and-Parmesan-Cheese-236494\">this one</a>&nbsp;using Parmesan cheese, mushrooms, onions, celery, and bell peppers.</p> \n<p><strong>7. Breakfast Calzone</strong></p> \n<p>Wrap cooked ground sausage, ricotta, onion, shredded Parmesan, and mozzarella in a bit of pizza dough and bake the whole shebang for eight to 12 minutes at&nbsp;400 degrees. You’ll forget that calzones are associated with any other meal.</p> \n<p><strong>8. Doctor your&nbsp;<a href=\"http://allrecipes.com/recipe/scones/\">standard scone recipe</a>&nbsp;by adding cheddar cheese and chopped chives; just remember to leave out the sugar.</p> \n<p><strong>9. Savory Oatmeal</strong></p> \n<p>Newsflash: oatmeal doesn’t always have to be sweet. Add the mixture to a Country Crock Simply Delicious<em>–</em>greased skillet and stir until it’s cooked thoroughly.           var swf = "      \u003cembed type=\"application\/x-shockwave-flash\"     s\u0072c=\"http:\/\/s.ytimg.com\/yts\/swfbin\/player-vflISCIWj\/watch_as3.swf\"     name=\"movie_player\"     id=\"movie_player\"    flashvars=\"__flashvars__\"     allowfullscreen=\"true\" allowscriptaccess=\"always\" bgcolor=\"#000000\"\u003e\n  \u003cnoembed\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"yt-alert yt-alert-default yt-alert-error  yt-alert-player\"\u003e  \u003cdiv class=\"yt-alert-icon\"\u003e\n    \u003cimg s\u0072c=\"http:\/\/s.ytimg.com\/yts\/img\/pixel-vfl3z5WfW.gif\" class=\"icon master-sprite\" alt=\"Alert icon\"\u003e\n  \u003c\/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"yt-alert-buttons\"\u003e\u003c\/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"yt-alert-content\" role=\"alert\"\u003e    \u003cspan class=\"yt-alert-vertical-trick\"\u003e\u003c\/span\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"yt-alert-message\"\u003e\n            You need Adobe Flash Player to watch this video. \u003cbr\u003e \u003ca href=\"http:\/\/get.adobe.com\/flashplayer\/\"\u003eDownload it from Adobe.\u003c\/a\u003e\n    \u003c\/div\u003e\n\u003c\/div\u003e\u003c\/div\u003e\u003c\/noembed\u003e\n\n";
          swf = swf.replace('__flashvars__', encoded.join('&'));
          document.getElementById("player-api").innerHTML = swf;
          ytplayer.config.loaded = true
        })();
      </script>

             <div id="watch-description" class="yt-uix-expander yt-uix-expander-collapsed yt-uix-button-panel"> 
              <div id="watch-description-content"> 
               <div id="watch-description-clip"> 
                <p id="watch-uploader-info"> <strong>Published on <span id="eow-date" class="watch-video-date">Mar 5, 2014</span> </strong> </p> 
                <div id="watch-description-text"> 
                 <p id="eow-description">Nosang Myung, a chemical and environmental engineering professor at the University of California, Riverside, invented the &quot;electronic nose.&quot; It's a tiny nanosensor that detects chemical compounds in the air. The most recent version, developed by Nano Engineered Applications, Inc., could be the basic platform for any number of applications that involve sniffing out airborne chemicals. &quot;Anything a nose can do, this can do,&quot; Myung says.<br /><br />Want the whole story? Read the Winter 2014 issue of UCR Magazine at <a href="http://magazine.ucr.edu/158" target="_blank" title="http://magazine.ucr.edu/158" rel="nofollow" dir="ltr" class="yt-uix-redirect-link">http://magazine.ucr.edu/158</a>.</p> 
                </div>

     <div id="omnicontent"> 
      <!-- com.omniupdate.div label="home-image" group="Everyone" button="657" -->
      <!-- com.omniupdate.editor csspath="/z-omniupdate/css/style.css" cssmenu="/z-omniupdate/css/style.txt" width="484" -->
      <!-- /com.omniupdate.div --> 
      <!-- com.omniupdate.div label="maincontent" group="Everyone" button="657" -->
      <!-- com.omniupdate.editor csspath="/z-omniupdate/css/style.css" cssmenu="/z-omniupdate/css/style.txt" width="484" -->
      <p>The Data Control service is designed to provide special handling for the administrative user who needs individual attention for production runs. Data Control personnel will provide the following: schedule and monitor job processing, coordinate delays, verify job output, and arrange for the distribution of the output.</p> 
      <p>Contact <a href="mailto:datacontrol@ucr.edu">datacontrol@ucr.edu</a></p>
